% Custom commands for story placement using TikZ for rounded corners
\newcommand{\storybox}[3]{% #1=x, #2=y, #3=text
  \begin{textblock}{3}(#1,#2)
    \noindent%
    \begin{tikzpicture}
      \node[rectangle, rounded corners=3pt, fill=white, inner sep=0.1in, text width=2.55in, align=left] {%
        \small\sffamily #3%
      };
    \end{tikzpicture}%
  \end{textblock}%
}

{\Large\sffamily A Speculative Atlas of Climate Disaster}

\vspace{0.5in}

{\large\sffamily A Procedurally Generated Novel}

\vspace{1in}

{\large\sffamily by Mark Sample}

\vfill

{\normalsize\sffamily Generated November 24, 2025}

\end{titlepage}

% About page
\newpage
\section*{About This Novel}

\noindent\textit{No Time to Discourse} is a speculative atlas that explores climate disaster across North America through interactive mapping and generative flash fiction.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent This novel was generated for NaNoGenMo (National Novel Generation Month), transforming the web-based interactive experience of https://notime.now/ into a print format. Each page combines watercolor maps from Stamen Design with works of flash fiction, which are procedurally-generated through bespoke RiTa.js grammars developed by Mark Sample.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent Each of the stories in this novel is a work of fiction, yet each also attempts to capture at a human level the realities of climate disaster.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent\textbf{Original Web Project:} \url{https://notime.now/}

\noindent\textbf{Code Repository:} \url{https://github.com/samplereality/no-time-to-discourse-novel}

\clearpage

% Henry V quote on its own page
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
  {\Large\textit{"The day is hot, and the weather, and the wars, and the King,\\
  and the Dukes; it is no time to discourse."}}

  \vspace{0.3in}

  --- Henry V
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\storybox{3.44}{7.92}{\textbf{Waterbury, Connecticut}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Sunday, March 8, 2026}\\
 The storm isn't even over before the river bursts its banks, the water rising 39 feet and swamping parts of Waterbury. It's bad enough when Barbara sees Fulton Park wash away, but then she hears on the news about the preschool. Twenty-four dead.}

\storybox{2.11}{4.74}{\textbf{New Haven, Connecticut}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, January 26, 2026}\\
 It stormed for days, the rain pouring down like blood gushing from an open wound. In the end, Zander's home was utterly destroyed, and there's only so much a GoFundMe can do.}

\storybox{0.40}{0.40}{\textbf{Bridgeport, Connecticut}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Sunday, November 4, 2029}\\
 ``You could fry an egg on the sidewalk,'' they say. No. Not when the sidewalk itself is melting. The November heat hits Cherish fast and hard. Fatigue, seizures. Nonsense thoughts drift through her head. \textit{Levi's 501, Bristol Myers Squibb, Bizarre Insurances.}}

\storybox{2.78}{6.29}{\textbf{Harlingen, Texas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Wednesday, November 14, 2029}\\
 Far out of sight a pressure surge triggered a chain reaction on the Black Tide platform. An unstoppable flow of crude poured into the coastal waters, a spill the size of a small state. Jaelyn has nightmares about broken clocks floating in oil-slicked waters.}

\storybox{1.48}{3.11}{\textbf{Brownsville, Texas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Tuesday, January 25, 2028}\\
 Hurricane Katie roared ashore as a Category 5 monster, following the path forecasters feared most. Katie evacuated to a Red Cross evacuation center with photo albums and medication. She refreshed the weather app every few minutes, wondering if her vintage vinyl collection would survive. The storm left behind a landscape of snapped power lines and roofless houses. She couldn't stop refreshing the missing persons list, looking for names she recognized.}
